<p><b>Daytona International Speedway</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Race_track" title="Race track">race track</a> in <a href="/wiki/Daytona_Beach,_Florida" title="Daytona Beach, Florida">Daytona Beach, Florida</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.  Since opening in 1959, it has been the home of the <a href="/wiki/Daytona_500" title="Daytona 500">Daytona 500</a>, the most prestigious race in <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a>. In addition to NASCAR, the track also hosts races of <a href="/wiki/Automobile_Racing_Club_of_America" title="Automobile Racing Club of America">ARCA</a>, <a href="/wiki/AMA_Superbike" class="mw-redirect" title="AMA Superbike">AMA Superbike</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Motor_Sports_Association" title="International Motor Sports Association">IMSA</a>, <a href="/wiki/SCCA" class="mw-redirect" title="SCCA">SCCA</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Motocross" title="Motocross">Motocross</a>. The track features multiple layouts including the primary 2.5-mile (4.0&#160;km) high-speed <a href="/wiki/Tri-oval" title="Tri-oval">tri-oval</a>, a 3.56-mile (5.73&#160;km) <a href="/wiki/Sports_car" title="Sports car">sports car</a> course, a 2.95-mile (4.75&#160;km) motorcycle course, and a 1,320-foot (400&#160;m) karting and motorcycle flat-track. The track's 180-acre (73&#160;ha) infield includes the 29-acre (12&#160;ha) <a href="/wiki/Lake_Lloyd" class="mw-redirect" title="Lake Lloyd">Lake Lloyd</a>, which has hosted <a href="/wiki/Powerboat" class="mw-redirect" title="Powerboat">powerboat</a> racing. The speedway is owned and operated by <a href="/wiki/International_Speedway_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="International Speedway Corporation">International Speedway Corporation</a>.
</p><p>The track was built in 1959 by NASCAR founder <a href="/wiki/Bill_France_Sr." title="Bill France Sr.">William "Bill" France, Sr.</a> to host racing that was held at the former <a href="/wiki/Daytona_Beach_Road_Course" class="mw-redirect" title="Daytona Beach Road Course">Daytona Beach Road Course</a>. His banked design permitted higher speeds and gave fans a better view of the cars. Lights were installed around the track in 1998, and today it is the third-largest single lit outdoor sports facility. The speedway has been renovated four times, with the infield renovated in 2004 and the track repaved in 1978 and 2010. The track is 50 miles north of <a href="/wiki/Orlando" class="mw-redirect" title="Orlando">Orlando</a>.
</p><p>On January 22, 2013, the fourth speedway renovation was unveiled. On July 5, 2013, ground was broken on "Daytona Rising" to remove backstretch seating and completely redevelop the frontstretch seating. The renovation was by design-builder Barton Malow Company in partnership with Rossetti Architects. The project was completed in January 2016, and cost <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US $</a>400&#160;million. It emphasized improved fan experience with five expanded and redesigned fan entrances (called "injectors"), as well as wider and more comfortable seats, and more restrooms and concession stands. After the renovations were complete, the track's grandstands had 101,000 permanent seats with the ability to increase permanent seating to 125,000.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-daytonarising_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daytonarising-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The project was finished before the start of Speedweek in 2016.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Track_history">Track history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Track history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> founder <a href="/wiki/William_France_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="William France Sr.">William France Sr.</a> began planning for the track in 1953 as a way to promote the series, which at the time was racing on the <a href="/wiki/Daytona_Beach_Road_Course" class="mw-redirect" title="Daytona Beach Road Course">Daytona Beach Road Course</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hawkins&#160;—_Tales_from_500_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hawkins_—_Tales_from_500-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> France met with Daytona Beach engineer Charles Moneypenny to discuss his plans for the speedway. He wanted the track to have the highest banking possible to allow the cars to reach high speeds and to give fans a better view of the cars on track. Moneypenny traveled to <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, Michigan to visit the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Proving_Grounds" title="Ford Proving Grounds">Ford Proving Grounds</a> which had a high-speed test track with banked corners. Ford shared their engineering design of the track with Moneypenny, providing the needed details of how to transition the pavement from a flat straightaway to a banked corner. France took the plans to the Daytona Beach city commission, who supported his idea and formed the Daytona Beach Speedway Authority.<sup id="cite_ref-created_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-created-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Daytona_International_Speedway_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Daytona_International_Speedway_2011.jpg/200px-Daytona_International_Speedway_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Daytona_International_Speedway_2011.jpg/300px-Daytona_International_Speedway_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Daytona_International_Speedway_2011.jpg/400px-Daytona_International_Speedway_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Daytona_International_Speedway_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The tri-oval after the 2010–2011 repaving</div></div></div>
<p>The city commission agreed to lease the 447-acre (181&#160;<a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">ha</a>) parcel of land adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Daytona_Beach_International_Airport" title="Daytona Beach International Airport">Daytona Beach Municipal Airport</a> to France's corporation for $10,000 a year over a 50-year period. France then began working on building funding for the project and found support from a <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> oil millionaire, <a href="/wiki/Clint_Murchison,_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="Clint Murchison, Sr.">Clint Murchison, Sr.</a> Murchison lent France $600,000 along with the construction equipment necessary to build the track. France also secured funding from <a href="/wiki/Pepsi-Cola" class="mw-redirect" title="Pepsi-Cola">Pepsi-Cola</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> designer <a href="/wiki/Harley_Earl" title="Harley Earl">Harley Earl</a>, a second mortgage on his home and selling 300,000 stock shares to local residents. Ground broke on construction of the 2.5-mile (4.0&#160;km) speedway on November 25, 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-created_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-created-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To build the high banking, crews had to excavate over a million square yards of soil from the track's infield.<sup id="cite_ref-Star01-04-1959_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Star01-04-1959-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Because of the high water table in the area, the excavated hole filled with water to form what is now known as Lake Lloyd, named after Joseph "Sax" Lloyd, one of the original six members of the Daytona Beach Speedway Authority. (The lake was stocked with 65,000 fish, and France arranged <a href="/wiki/Speedboat" class="mw-redirect" title="Speedboat">speedboat</a> races on it.)<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> 22 tons of <a href="/wiki/Lime_mortar" title="Lime mortar">lime mortar</a> had to be brought in to form the track's <a href="/wiki/Base_course" title="Base course">binding base</a>, over which <a href="/wiki/Asphalt" title="Asphalt">asphalt</a> was laid. Because of the extreme degree of banking, Moneypenny had to come up with a way to pave the incline. He connected the paving equipment to bulldozers anchored at the top of the banking. This allowed the paving equipment to pave the banking without slipping or rolling down the incline. Moneypenny subsequently patented his construction method<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and later designed <a href="/wiki/Talladega_Superspeedway" title="Talladega Superspeedway">Talladega Superspeedway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michigan_International_Speedway" title="Michigan International Speedway">Michigan International Speedway</a>. By December 1958, France had begun to run out of money and relied on race ticket sales to complete construction.<sup id="cite_ref-created_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-created-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Daytona_International_Speedway_on_the_day_of_the_Daytona_500.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Daytona_International_Speedway_on_the_day_of_the_Daytona_500.JPG/200px-Daytona_International_Speedway_on_the_day_of_the_Daytona_500.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Daytona_International_Speedway_on_the_day_of_the_Daytona_500.JPG/300px-Daytona_International_Speedway_on_the_day_of_the_Daytona_500.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Daytona_International_Speedway_on_the_day_of_the_Daytona_500.JPG/400px-Daytona_International_Speedway_on_the_day_of_the_Daytona_500.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Daytona_International_Speedway_on_the_day_of_the_Daytona_500.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The tri-oval during the <a href="/wiki/2015_Daytona_500" title="2015 Daytona 500">2015 Daytona 500</a> with nearly completed grandstand in the background.</div></div></div>
<p>The first practice run on the new track was on February 6, 1959. On February 22, 1959, 42,000 people attended the inaugural Daytona 500.<sup id="cite_ref-created_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-created-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Its finish was as startling as the track itself: <a href="/wiki/Lee_Petty" title="Lee Petty">Lee Petty</a> beat <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Beauchamp" title="Johnny Beauchamp">Johnny Beauchamp</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Photo_finish" title="Photo finish">photo finish</a> that took three days to adjudicate.<sup id="cite_ref-Kettlewell,_p.503_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kettlewell,_p.503-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> When the track opened it was the fastest race track to host a stock car race, until <a href="/wiki/Talladega_Superspeedway" title="Talladega Superspeedway">Talladega Superspeedway</a> opened 10 years later.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On April 4, it hosted a 100&#160;mi (160&#160;km) <a href="/wiki/Champ_Car" class="mw-redirect" title="Champ Car">Champ Car</a> event which saw <a href="/wiki/Jim_Rathmann" title="Jim Rathmann">Jim Rathmann</a> beat <a href="/wiki/Dick_Rathmann" title="Dick Rathmann">Dick Rathmann</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rodger_Ward" title="Rodger Ward">Rodger Ward</a>, at an average speed of 170.26&#160;mph (274.01&#160;km/h), at the time the fastest motor race ever.<sup id="cite_ref-Kettlewell,_p.503_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kettlewell,_p.503-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> It was sadly the occasion of Daytona's first fatality: <a href="/wiki/George_Amick" title="George Amick">George Amick</a>, attempting to overtake for third late in the race, hit a wall and was killed.<sup id="cite_ref-Kettlewell,_p.503_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kettlewell,_p.503-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> April 5, a scheduled 1,000&#160;km (620&#160;mi) <a href="/wiki/Sports_car_racing" title="Sports car racing">sports car</a> event (shortened to 560&#160;mi (900&#160;km) by darkness) was won by <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Mieres" title="Roberto Mieres">Roberto Mieres</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fritz_d%27Orey" title="Fritz d&#39;Orey">Fritz d'Orey</a>, who shared a <a href="/wiki/Porsche_718" title="Porsche 718">Porsche RSK</a>, which proved more durable than more potent competition.<sup id="cite_ref-Kettlewell,_p.503_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kettlewell,_p.503-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lights were installed around the track in 1998 to run NASCAR's July race, the <a href="/wiki/Coke_Zero_400" class="mw-redirect" title="Coke Zero 400">Coke Zero 400</a> at night. The track was the world's largest single lighted outdoor sports facility until being surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Losail_International_Circuit" title="Losail International Circuit">Losail International Circuit</a> in 2008.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/Musco_Lighting" title="Musco Lighting">Musco Lighting</a> installed the lighting system, which took into account glare and visibility for aircraft arriving and departing nearby Daytona Beach International Airport, and costs about $240 per hour when in operation.<sup id="cite_ref-musco_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-musco-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Layouts">Layouts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Layouts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tri-Oval">Tri-Oval</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Tri-Oval">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Daytona_International_Speedway.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Daytona_International_Speedway.svg/220px-Daytona_International_Speedway.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Daytona_International_Speedway.svg/330px-Daytona_International_Speedway.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Daytona_International_Speedway.svg/440px-Daytona_International_Speedway.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1255" data-file-height="672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Daytona_International_Speedway.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the speedway</div></div></div>
<p>Daytona's <a href="/wiki/Tri-oval" title="Tri-oval">tri-oval</a> is 2.5 miles (4.0&#160;km) long with 31° banking in the turns and 18° banking at the start/finish line.  The front straight is 3,800 feet (1,200&#160;m) long and the back straight (or "superstretch") is 3,000 feet (910&#160;m) long.  The tri-oval shape was revolutionary at the time as it greatly improved sight lines for fans. It is one of the two tracks on the NASCAR Cup Series circuit that uses <a href="/wiki/Restrictor_plate" title="Restrictor plate">restrictor plates</a> to slow the cars down due to the high speeds, the other being <a href="/wiki/Talladega_Superspeedway" title="Talladega Superspeedway">Talladega Superspeedway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-trackfacts_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trackfacts-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 15, 2010, repaving of the track began. This came almost a year earlier than planned due to the track coming apart during the <a href="/wiki/2010_Daytona_500" title="2010 Daytona 500">2010 Daytona 500</a>. The project used an estimated 50,000 tons<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="This information is too vague. (April 2014)">vague</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> of asphalt to repave 1.4&#160;million square feet (130,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) including the racing surface, apron, skid pads and pit road. Because of good weather, the project was completed ahead of schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-goodyear_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-goodyear-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 9, 2013, <a href="/wiki/Colin_Braun" title="Colin Braun">Colin Braun</a> drove a <a href="/wiki/Daytona_Prototype" title="Daytona Prototype">Daytona Prototype</a> car prepared by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Shank_Racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael Shank Racing">Michael Shank Racing</a> to set a single-lap record on the tri-oval configuration of 222.971 miles per hour (358.837&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> During NASCAR Events, it takes less than a minute for the cars to complete a lap around the 2.5-mile tri-oval course.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Road_courses">Road courses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Road courses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Road_Course.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Road_Course.svg/220px-Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Road_Course.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Road_Course.svg/330px-Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Road_Course.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Road_Course.svg/440px-Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Road_Course.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1281" data-file-height="710" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Road_Course.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the 24-hour road course configuration</div></div></div>
<p>The 3.81-mile (6.13&#160;km) road course was built in 1959 and first hosted a three-hour sports car race called the Daytona Continental in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The race length became 2,000&#160;km (1,200&#160;mi) in 1964,<sup id="cite_ref-Kettlewell,_p.503_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kettlewell,_p.503-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and in 1966 was extended to a 24-hour endurance race known as the <a href="/wiki/Rolex_24_at_Daytona" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolex 24 at Daytona">Rolex 24 at Daytona</a>. It was shortened again to six hours in 1972 and the 1974 rendition of the race was cancelled entirely.<sup id="cite_ref-Kettlewell,_p.503_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kettlewell,_p.503-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1973, a sharp chicane was added at the end of the backstretch, approaching oval turn three.
</p><p>In 1984<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and 1985,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> the layout was modified, re-profiling turns 1 and 2, and moving what is now turn 3 closer to its adjacent turns. In addition, the chicane on the backstretch was modified. A new entry leg was constructed approximately 400 feet (120&#160;m) earlier, resulting in a longer, three-legged, "bus stop" shape. Cars would now enter in the first leg, bypass the second leg, and exit out of the existing third leg. Passing would now be possible inside the longer chicane. The construction resulted in a final length of 3.56 miles (5.73&#160;km) for the complete road course.
</p><p>In 2003, the chicane was modified once again. The middle leg was repaved and widened, and now cars would enter through the first leg, and exit out of the second leg. The existing third leg was abandoned. This allowed cars a cleaner entry into oval turn three. After favorable results, in 2010 the third leg was dug up, and removed permanently.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2011_Rolex_24_Hours_of_Daytona_start.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/2011_Rolex_24_Hours_of_Daytona_start.png/220px-2011_Rolex_24_Hours_of_Daytona_start.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/2011_Rolex_24_Hours_of_Daytona_start.png/330px-2011_Rolex_24_Hours_of_Daytona_start.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/2011_Rolex_24_Hours_of_Daytona_start.png/440px-2011_Rolex_24_Hours_of_Daytona_start.png 2x" data-file-width="970" data-file-height="644" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2011_Rolex_24_Hours_of_Daytona_start.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Start of the 2011 Rolex 24 at Daytona</div></div></div>
<p>While the more famous <a href="/wiki/24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="24 Hours of Le Mans">24 Hours of Le Mans</a> is held near the <a href="/wiki/Summer_solstice" title="Summer solstice">summer solstice</a>, Daytona's endurance race is held in winter (meaning more of the race is run at night). The track's lighting system is limited to 20% of its maximum output for the race to keep cars dependent on their headlights.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Moto_Course.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Moto_Course.png/220px-Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Moto_Course.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Moto_Course.png/330px-Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Moto_Course.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Moto_Course.png/440px-Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Moto_Course.png 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1518" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Daytona_International_Speedway_-_Moto_Course.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Moto-Course</div></div></div>
<p>In 2005, a second infield road course configuration was constructed, primarily <a href="/wiki/Daytona_200" title="Daytona 200">for motorcycles</a>. Due to fears of tire wear on the banked oval sections, oval turns 1 and 2 were bypassed giving the new course a length of 2.95 miles (4.75&#160;km). The Daytona SportBike that runs the Daytona 200 however, uses the main road course except for the motorcycle <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Rodr%C3%ADguez_(racing_driver)" title="Pedro Rodríguez (racing driver)">Pedro Rodríguez</a> Hairpin (tighter than the one used for cars; the car version is used as an acceleration lane for motorcycles).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 26 and 27, 2006, the <a href="/wiki/IndyCar_Series" title="IndyCar Series">IndyCar Series</a> held a compatibility test on the 10-turn, 2.73-mile (4.39&#160;km) modified road course, and the 12-turn 2.95-mile (4.75&#160;km) motorcycle road course with 5 drivers. The drivers who tested at the track were <a href="/wiki/Vitor_Meira" class="mw-redirect" title="Vitor Meira">Vitor Meira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Hornish_Jr." title="Sam Hornish Jr.">Sam Hornish Jr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Kanaan" title="Tony Kanaan">Tony Kanaan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Dixon" title="Scott Dixon">Scott Dixon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dan_Wheldon" title="Dan Wheldon">Dan Wheldon</a>. This marked the first time since 1984 that open wheel cars have taken to the track at Daytona.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> On January 31&#160;– February 1, 2007, IndyCar returned for a full test involving 17 cars.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Supercross">Supercross</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Supercross">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/Daytona_Beach_Bike_Week" title="Daytona Beach Bike Week">Daytona Beach Bike Week</a>, a supercross track is built between pit road and the tri-oval section of the track.  Historically the track has used more sand than dirt, providing unique challenges to riders.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The 2008–2013 track configurations were designed by former champion, <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Carmichael" title="Ricky Carmichael">Ricky Carmichael</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Daytona has hosted an <a href="/wiki/AMA_Supercross_Championship" title="AMA Supercross Championship">AMA Supercross Championship</a> round uninterruptedly since 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Daytona_Flat_Track_and_Infield_Kart_Track">Daytona Flat Track and Infield Kart Track</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Daytona Flat Track and Infield Kart Track">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Popular dirt-track races in karting and flat-track motorcycle racing had been held at <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Stadium_(Daytona_Beach)" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipal Stadium (Daytona Beach)">Daytona Beach Municipal Stadium</a> but in 2009, the city announced the stadium was replacing its entire surface with <a href="/wiki/FieldTurf" title="FieldTurf">FieldTurf</a>, and thereby eliminating the flat-track racing at the stadium. To continue racing, speedway officials built the Daytona Flat Track, a new quarter-mile dirt track outside of turns 1 &amp; 2 of the main superspeedway. It seats 5,000 in temporary grandstands and opened in December 2009 for WKA KartWeek.  From 2010 to 2016, it also hosted the <a href="/wiki/AMA_Grand_National_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="AMA Grand National Championship">AMA Grand National Championship</a>, before it was moved in 2017 to the tri-oval section and became a TT course.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There is also a short paved kart/autocross track in the infield just inside of turn 3. The <a href="/wiki/SCCA" class="mw-redirect" title="SCCA">SCCA</a> holds autocross on this track in addition to hosting sprint karting races during KartWeek.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Short_track">Short track</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Short track">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 2012, it was announced that a 0.4-mile (0.64&#160;km) <a href="/wiki/Short_track_motor_racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Short track motor racing">short track</a> would be constructed along the backstretch of the Speedway's main course, for NASCAR's lower-tier series to compete at during Speedweeks called the <a href="/wiki/UNOH_Battle_at_the_Beach" title="UNOH Battle at the Beach">UNOH Battle at the Beach</a>, which is similar to the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_All-Star_Showdown" title="Toyota All-Star Showdown">Toyota All-Star Showdown</a>, formerly held at <a href="/wiki/Irwindale_Speedway" class="mw-redirect" title="Irwindale Speedway">Irwindale Speedway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The first races were held on that track in February 2013. The track was shortened to 1,980-foot (603.50&#160;m) oval in 2014 by shorter straightaways. The future of racing at the short track is unknown after 2015 with the grandstands on the back straightaway being demolished as a part of the Daytona Rising project.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the fall of 1959, the track hosted several high school football games for the <a href="/wiki/Father_Lopez_Catholic_High_School" title="Father Lopez Catholic High School">Father Lopez Green Wave</a> in their first year of their football program.
</p><p>The track hosted four <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a> games featuring the Daytona-based <a href="/wiki/Bethune%E2%80%93Cookman_Wildcats" title="Bethune–Cookman Wildcats">Bethune–Cookman Wildcats</a> in 1974 and 1975. In early 2014 track president Joie Chitwood expressed a desire to bring football back to the track.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1994, <a href="/wiki/Sega" title="Sega">Sega</a> released an arcade game called <i><a href="/wiki/Daytona_USA_(video_game)" title="Daytona USA (video game)">Daytona USA</a></i>, using their Model 2 Arcade hardware. It was developed by their famed "AM2" development team. It featured a fully detailed 3D model of the circuit for the very first time. The soundtrack for the game included vocals by <a href="/wiki/Takenobu_Mitsuyoshi" title="Takenobu Mitsuyoshi">Takenobu Mitsuyoshi</a>. It is widely considered to be one of the most successful and influential racing games of all time. <i>Daytona USA</i> spawned many sequels, both in the arcades and on various home videogame consoles. The latest version, <i>Daytona Championship USA</i>, was released to arcades in 2017.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/IRacing.com" class="mw-redirect" title="IRacing.com">iRacing.com</a> have laser-scanned the facility twice. The first in 2008, and 2011 once the repave was completed. Both are available in official racing series. There has been no word to when and if it will be re-scanned now that the Daytona Rising project has now been completed.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Both the oval layout and Rolex 24 Hour layout are available in both <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a> video games <i><a href="/wiki/Gran_Turismo_5" title="Gran Turismo 5">Gran Turismo 5</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Gran_Turismo_6" title="Gran Turismo 6">Gran Turismo 6</a></i>. Daytona International Speedway is also featured in <i><a href="/wiki/Forza_Motorsport_6" title="Forza Motorsport 6">Forza Motorsport 6</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Forza_Motorsport_7" title="Forza Motorsport 7">Forza Motorsport 7</a></i> for the Xbox One and Windows 10.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Real_Racing_3" title="Real Racing 3">Real Racing 3</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s second NASCAR update featured the Daytona International Speedway as a new circuit coming in three layouts. In addition to the oval and Rolex 24 Hour layouts in <i>Gran Turismo</i>, there also exists a Daytona 200 layout in the game.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fatalities">Fatalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fatalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Daytona_International_Speedway_fatalities" title="List of Daytona International Speedway fatalities">List of Daytona International Speedway fatalities</a></div>
<p>40 people have been fatally injured in on-track incidents: 23 car drivers, twelve motorcyclists, three go-kart drivers, one powerboat racer, and one track worker. The most notorious death may have been that of <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt" title="Dale Earnhardt">Dale Earnhardt</a>, who <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Dale_Earnhardt" title="Death of Dale Earnhardt">was killed</a> on the last lap of the <a href="/wiki/2001_Daytona_500" title="2001 Daytona 500">2001 Daytona 500</a> on February 18, 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fan_amenities">Fan amenities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Fan amenities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Earnhardt_Grandstand.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Earnhardt_Grandstand.jpg/220px-Earnhardt_Grandstand.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Earnhardt_Grandstand.jpg/330px-Earnhardt_Grandstand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Earnhardt_Grandstand.jpg/440px-Earnhardt_Grandstand.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Earnhardt_Grandstand.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The former Earnhardt Grandstand at Daytona International Speedway, which was changed into one of the injectors after Daytona Rising</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UNOH_Fanzone">UNOH Fanzone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: UNOH Fanzone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b>UNOH Fanzone</b> is an access package similar to pit passes for fans to get closer to drivers and race teams. The fanzone was built in 2004 as part of a renovation of the track's infield.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Fans are able to walk on top of the garages, known as the "fandeck", and view track and garage activity. Fans can also view race teams working in the garage, including NASCAR technical inspection, through windows. The garage windows also include slots for fans to hand merchandise to drivers for autographs. The fanzone also includes a live entertainment stage, additional food and drink areas and various other activities and displays.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2004 renovation of the infield, headed by design firm <a href="/wiki/HNTB" title="HNTB">HNTB</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> was the first major renovation of the infield in the history of the track.<sup id="cite_ref-aia-award_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aia-award-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the fanzone, a new vehicle and pedestrian tunnel was built under turn 1.  The tunnel posed a challenge to engineers because it was to be built under the water table. Another challenge came during construction when three named hurricanes passed by the track, flooding much of the excavation work. The infield renovation involved landscaping and hardscaping, such as a new walkway along the shore of Lake Lloyd, and the construction of 34 new buildings, including garages and fueling stations, offices and inspection facilities, and a club. The renovation project received a 2005 Award for Excellence from Design-Build Institute of America.<sup id="cite_ref-aia-award_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aia-award-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Following the success of the UNOH Fanzone at Daytona, <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Motor_Speedway" title="Las Vegas Motor Speedway">Las Vegas Motor Speedway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kansas_Speedway" title="Kansas Speedway">Kansas Speedway</a> each built a similar infield fanzone.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On December 9, 2016, the speedway announced that the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Northwestern_Ohio" title="University of Northwestern Ohio">University of Northwestern Ohio</a> purchased entitlement rights to the fanzone, and that the area will be named 'UNOH Fanzone'.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Budweiser_Party_Porch">Budweiser Party Porch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Budweiser Party Porch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b>Budweiser Party Porch</b> was a 46-foot-high (14&#160;m) porch located along the backstretch of the track. It was built on top of a portion of the backstretch grandstands and includes a 277-foot-wide (84&#160;m), 33-foot-tall (10&#160;m) sign, the largest sign in motorsports.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The porch featured tables, food and drinks, offering fans a "fun-filled" atmosphere that breaks fans away from the confines of grandstand seating without sacrificing on the view. Below the porch was an interactive fan zone featuring amusement rides, a go-kart track, show cars and merchandise trailers.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> After the 2015 racing season, the Party Porch was torn down with the backstretch grandstands as part of the DAYTONA Rising project.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current">Current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former">Former</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Former">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Weather_and_climate">Weather and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Daytona_International_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Weather and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Daytona has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>Cfa</i>), which enables year-round use of the facility. Light frosts are in theory possible, but unlikely, during the 24-hour event's night-time under clear conditions, but general racing conditions are mild also during winter. With a dry season taking place during winter months, the 500 generally has good odds at being run without rain delays. The summer event under the floodlights is more likely to undergo disturbances, due to the rainy tendencies of the hot, muggy and humid summers. Due to the complete difference of seasons, the two NASCAR Cup races at Daytona see vastly different track conditions.
</p>
